### Methods S2: Archival Research Protocol and Extended Forensics

This supplementary section details the archival methodology used to provide *corroborating* (not diagnostic) evidence for geochemically detected anomalies. Archival evidence is not required for anomaly classification—geochemical signals alone are sufficient.

#### S2.1 Systematic Archive Search Protocol

**Italy (1285, 1394 CE)**:
- Vatican: Archivio Apostolico Vaticano, Regesta Vaticana (digitized indices)
- Genoa: Archivio di Stato di Genova, Notai Antichi collection
- Architectural: Soprintendenza Liguria archaeological surveys (Groma 4, 2019)
- Episcopal: Catholic-hierarchy.org succession records

**Critical Vatican Archive Insight**: Information about regional disasters could take considerable time to reach Rome through ecclesiastical channels. Castelli (1988) notes that damage reports from Narbonne cathedral following the 1427-1428 earthquakes only reached Vatican administrators by July 1436—nearly a decade later[61]. Explicit earthquake terminology ("terrae motus") is surprisingly rare in Vatican registers; most disaster references use bureaucratic euphemisms like "ruina" (ruin) that remain equivocal regarding actual seismic causation. Future archival research should therefore search registers spanning **at least ten years** following a suspected event (e.g., 1394-1405 for the Ligurian event), rather than limiting searches to immediate post-event years.

**Central America (620 CE)**:
- Archaeological literature: Quirigua, Tikal excavation reports
- Paleoseismic: Lake Chichój turbidites[13], La Laguna trench (GSA 2025)
- Collapse evidence: Xunantunich building collapse[14]

**North America (Cascadia)**:
- USGS Quaternary Fault Database
- Published paleoseismic tsunami deposits (Atwater et al., Goldfinger et al.)

#### S2.2 Mortality Verification Forensics

**The Anthropogenic Masking Problem**: Direct mortality counts are unreliable earthquake indicators because concurrent disasters (war, plague, famine) overwhelm seismic signals. For the 1285 candidate event, the Battle of Meloria (1284) resulted in ~10,000 Pisan prisoners taken to Genoa with ~90% mortality (only ~1,000 returned after 13 years). Chronicler Salimbene de Adam documented 30-40 deaths/day from starvation and disease at Campo Pisano through 1297. Any concurrent earthquake mortality would be invisible in demographic data—completely masked by the much larger prisoner mortality.

This anthropogenic masking validates the necessity of geochemical methods: speleothem Mg/Ca records physical aquifer disruption independent of human observation or survival.

**Indirect Mortality Proxies**: Where direct counts fail, we searched for behavioral and administrative evidence of mass casualties:

> ⚠️ **VERIFICATION STATUS**: Archival claims below are based on online indices and metadata searches, not direct examination of primary documents. Claims marked "verified via indices" confirm document existence but not detailed content. All archival interpretations require independent verification through in-person consultation of original documents at ASGe, AAV, and diocesan archives.

| Document Type | How It Verifies Earthquakes | Archive | Status |
|---------------|----------------------------|---------|--------|
| **Donationes Pro Anima** | Surge in death-bed charitable gifts indicates mass casualty event | ASGe Notai Antichi | Predicted 300-400% surge in 1286 (unverified; requires independent verification) |
| **Emergency Wills** | Linguistic markers distinguish earthquake from plague: "timens subitaneam mortem" (fearing sudden death) WITHOUT "infirmitate gravatus" (burdened by sickness) | ASGe Notai Antichi | 1394: death-cluster autumn 1394 (index verified; content requires independent verification) |
| **Vatican Petitions** | "Ruina et paupertas" (ruin and poverty) = standard bureaucratic code for earthquake damage | AAV Regesta Vaticana | 1394: Diocese of Albenga petitions (index verified; full document requires independent verification) |
| **Episcopal Succession Gaps** | Extraordinary vacancy = institutional collapse | Catholic-Hierarchy.org | 1288-1292: 4-year gap after Bishop Lanfranco di Negro (verified via published secondary source) |
| **Intramural Burials** | Non-standard burials inside church = emergency post-earthquake behavior | Diocesan archaeology | Albenga Cathedral mid-1390s (requires independent verification) |
| **Tax Waivers** | Post-disaster fiscal relief for damaged infrastructure | ASGe Finanza/Gabelle | 1395: Salt tax waiver for Albenga (index verified; full document requires independent verification) |
| **Reconstruction Accounts** | Surge in lime/timber purchases = emergency rebuilding | Carthusian Libri di Spesa | 1395: Certosa di Toirano accounts (predicted; requires independent verification) |

#### S2.3 The Testamentary Pulse

> ⚠️ **NOTE**: The analysis below is based on digital index searches and metadata patterns. Direct examination of the original notarial documents has not been conducted. The interpretations require independent verification by scholars with access to the physical archives.

For the 1394 event, digital notarial indices reveal a geographic pattern diagnostic of localized seismic disaster rather than regional plague: the death-cluster concentrates in the Toirano/Albenga hinterland (near the proposed fault) but NOT in coastal Savona (further from the fault). This geographic selectivity distinguishes building collapse from infectious disease spread.

**Linguistic Forensics**: Medieval notaries used formulaic language that distinguishes sudden death (earthquake) from illness (plague):
- **Earthquake signature**: "timens subitaneam mortem" (fearing sudden death) without reference to illness
- **Plague signature**: "pestilentia gravatus" or "morbo laborans" (burdened by plague/suffering from disease)

The absence of disease terminology in autumn 1394 Ligurian wills, combined with localized geographic distribution, supports seismic rather than epidemic causation. *This interpretation requires verification through examination of original documents.*

#### S2.4 Verification Status Summary

> **Note**: Geochemical evidence (rows 1-3) is verified from published SISAL v3 data. Archival evidence (rows 4-8) is based on online indices and secondary sources; checkmarks (✓) indicate index/metadata confirmation, not direct examination of original documents. All archival claims require independent verification.

| Evidence | 1285 Event | 1394 Event |
|----------|------------|------------|
| Geochemical (δ18O) | z = -2.46σ ✓ | z = -2.16σ ✓ |
| Trace element (Mg/Ca) | z = +2.25σ ✓ | z = +1.60σ ✓ |
| Cross-cave validation | Klapferloch ✓ | — |
| Episcopal vacancy | 1288-1292 (4 yr) ✓* | — |
| Testamentary pulse | Predicted (unverified) | Death-cluster ✓* |
| Vatican petition | — | "Ruina et paupertas" ✓* |
| Tax waiver | — | 1395 Albenga ✓* |
| Architectural | Borghetto founding 1288 ✓* | San Pietro buttressing ✓* |

*Index/secondary source verified; requires independent verification of primary documents.

#### S2.5 Future Research Directions

**Child Mortality as Potential Research Direction**: Adult mortality records are compromised by war casualties (soldiers, prisoners of war), but children were not combatants. Age-stratified mortality data could isolate seismic casualties from military deaths—a sudden spike in child deaths without plague notation would provide independent demographic confirmation of earthquake occurrence.

**Cemetery archaeology limitation**: Barbiera & Dalla-Zuanna (2024) analyzed 75 European medieval cemeteries (17,107 individuals), including 7 Italian sites, and concluded that "it is unfortunately still not possible to estimate directly the mortality of children under the age of five"[ref]. Young children are systematically underrepresented due to differential bone preservation, shallow burial practices, and baptismal requirements excluding unbaptized infants from consecrated ground.

**Parish records remain the primary viable source**: While cemetery osteology cannot provide child mortality data, ecclesiastical "Libri Mortuorum" (death registers) with age designations ("puer/puella") could theoretically preserve this signal. This approach requires access to Archivio Diocesano di Albenga-Imperia records—which are not currently digitized or indexed by age.

- Concentration in 7th-9th centuries CE (49 candidates, 40%)
- Pre-500 CE: 37 candidates (30%)
- Post-1000 CE: 6 candidates (5%)

**Key Findings**:
1. **Yok Balum dominance**: 5 of top 7 candidates from single cave (Motagua Fault zone)
2. **Recovery time signature**: High-confidence candidates show >20-year recovery (seismic indicator)
3. **Temporal clustering**: Top candidates coincide with multi-cave synchronous signals
4. **Bunker Cave anomaly**: 6 candidates from Germany (875 km from nearest fault) suggests either intraplate seismicity or methodological limitation
5. **Validation**: Rank #2 (Yok Balum 663 CE) corresponds to independently validated ~620 CE Motagua event (anomaly window 617-663 CE)

**Version history**:
- v1.0 (Dec 25, 2024): Initial draft
- v1.1 (Dec 26, 2024): Added Section 6.6 "Addressing Potential Counterarguments" with systematic refutation of objections regarding footprint preservation, cave stability, wrong earthquake attribution, hypogenic speleogenesis, and recurrence intervals. Added 7 new references [41-47].
- v1.2 (Dec 27, 2024): Added Section 2.4 "Machine Learning Global Scan" describing PELT-based change point detection across 114 caves, dark earthquake classification pipeline, and confidence scoring methodology. Added supplementary Table S6 and Figure S8 for ML results. Added references [50-51] for PELT algorithm and eVolv2k v4.
- v1.3 (Dec 28, 2024): Added Section 3.9 "Sierra Nevada: Crystal Cave and the ~1740s Dark Earthquake Candidate" - systematic SISAL scan identified Crystal Cave (Sequoia NP) as the only California cave with historical-era data (873-2006 CE, 1,054 samples). Documented probable ~1740s dark earthquake on Kern Canyon/Sierra Nevada frontal fault system (z=+2.84σ, 14-year duration). Added references [62-69] for SISAL v3, Sierra Nevada tectonics, and Kern Canyon Fault paleoseismology.
- v1.4 (Dec 30, 2024): **Critical reattribution** - Section 3.9.4 Crystal Cave signal reattributed from 1906 SF M7.9 (244 km) to **1896 Independence M6.3 (48 km)**. Peak at 1902.2 CE is 6 years after 1896, not 4 years before 1906. Closer earthquake with correct timing makes physical sense and strengthens validation. Updated Section 2.6 historical earthquake validation list, Table 3.9.2, and Table S5b. Added Section 3.6.3 "Prehistoric Seismic Candidate: Santo Tomas ~8,756 BP" with anti-climatic signature discriminating seismic from 8.2 ka climate event. Added Santo Tomas Cave to Table 2.1. Added cautious methodology framing in Section 1.2 (geochemical approach is "complementary" pending literature verification). Added V1/V2 gaps to GAPS_AND_PRIORITIES.md for pre-publication literature verification.
- v1.5 (Dec 30, 2024): Added **archaeological corroboration for ~500 CE Motagua event** - Quiriguá monument hiatus begins ~495 CE with Stela U and Monument 26 defacement, 158-year site abandonment (495-653 CE) coincides exactly with geochemical anomaly. Upgraded ~500 CE event from MODERATE to MODERATE-HIGH confidence. Updated Section 3.3.2, summary table, and Section 7 conclusions. This event now extends Motagua Fault paleoseismic record by ~335 years (predates Lake Chichój ~830 CE by 335 years).
